  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer769117385309614391">It was not Threadfall that made Menolly unhappy. It was her father who betrayed her ambition to be a Harper, who thwarted her love of music. Menolly had no choice but to run away. She came upon a group of fire lizards, wild relatives of the fire-breathing dragons. Her music swirled about them; she taught nine to sing, suddenly Menolly was no longer alone.</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1034862-what-is-threadfall">What is threadfall?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1034862'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F28541.Dragonsong">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1034862-what-is-threadfall">3 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1034862-what-is-threadfall">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/44312452-faerie"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/44312452-faerie">Faerie</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Dragonsong takes place on a made up planet. For anyone new to the series, I would describe it as fantasy, but in the later books it is more sci-fi ori<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Dragonsong takes place on a made up planet. For anyone new to the series, I would describe it as fantasy, but in the later books it is more sci-fi oriented.<br /><br />Essentially, thread is something which falls from space for fifty years which is referred to as a pass, periodically separated by a two-hundred year interval.<br /><br />It is an organism which eats anything organic and can only be nullified by fire, intense cold or full submersion in water. Extremely deadly. It is the reason dragons exist, and for context, this book is set during a pass.<br /><br />A pass is named such, because thread is commonly associated by something known as, "the red star." Later on, you find out that it is in actual fact, a planet, and has a bizarre orbit around the sun which will bring it further and closer from Pern in a cycle.<br /><br />ect, I could go on, but I don't want to confuse you with knowledge I haven't read up on for four years. The best way to find out more would be to dive into the series - it's pretty self explanatory and easy to pick up.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/391158-can-anyone-tell-me-what-role-music-played">Can anyone tell me what role music played in the daily life of pern? And why 
It&#39;s so important?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_391158'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F28541.Dragonsong">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/391158-can-anyone-tell-me-what-role-music-played">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/391158-can-anyone-tell-me-what-role-music-played">See all 2 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/44312452-faerie"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/44312452-faerie">Faerie</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Aside from thread, Pernese society and culture is very much based around music. They use songs to teach their children, ballads to record monumental, <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Aside from thread, Pernese society and culture is very much based around music. They use songs to teach their children, ballads to record monumental, historical events, music to liven up the dullness of ordinary life. They even use huge drums for long distance communication.<br /><br />The author spent nine years studying music, so it also happens to be a huge area of her interest and expertise - and anyone who's read a handful of her works will be able to tell that this also reflects in her writing.<br /><br />Dragonsong is the book which introduces Menolly, one of the characters at the forefront of the Harperhall and its chronicles. For a practical example, you would be best off reading Masterharper of Pern, for it tells the life of Robinton and touches on just about everything music has influenced in Pernese society - which is nearly everything in itself.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_5276008" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5276008" />
    <a title="Matthew Gatheringwater" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/298210-matthew-gatheringwater"><img alt="Matthew Gatheringwater" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1488077740p2/298210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5276008?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew Gatheringwater" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew Gatheringwater" href="/user/show/298210-matthew-gatheringwater">Matthew Gatheringwater</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553120448" href="/book/show/28543.Dragonsong">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/298210-matthew-gatheringwater?shelf=formative_fiction">formative_fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5276008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13419548675623999680">A book doesn't have to be Great Literature or even particularly good to appear on my "formative fiction" shelf, it just has to be a book with a meaning that changed me or helped me to understand myself and the world in a new way. Fortunately, <i>Dragonsong</i> is also a very good book of its type.<br/><br/>The best friend of my childhood was different from me in many ways: middle-class to my trailer-trash, older, weak where I was strong (he suffered from a heart condition that would kill him while still a teenag</span>
  <span id="freeText13419548675623999680" style="display:none">A book doesn't have to be Great Literature or even particularly good to appear on my "formative fiction" shelf, it just has to be a book with a meaning that changed me or helped me to understand myself and the world in a new way. Fortunately, <i>Dragonsong</i> is also a very good book of its type.<br /><br />The best friend of my childhood was different from me in many ways: middle-class to my trailer-trash, older, weak where I was strong (he suffered from a heart condition that would kill him while still a teenager), and part of a large and functioning family.<br /><br />We both lived in religious households that discouraged "worldly" reading but, while my folks were strict, his were lax. During a winter holiday sleep-over, he smuggled <i>Dragonsong</i> and some of its many sequels to me. We sprawled in front of the wood-stove and read all day and long into the night. I'd scrimped to save for treats and, feeling very elegant, served us Ritz crackers with Cheeze-Whiz (the big jar!) and vienna sausages. I was so anxious to impress, I put my finger on the side of the stove to show him how long I could stand to sizzle.<br /><br />There were other sleep-overs and other books, but this is was the important one, the one I remember whenever I open a new book and read merely for the pleasure of escape into another kind of life.<br /><br />Menolly, the protagonist of <i>Dragonsinger</i>, escapes in a more literal way. Denied the expression of her natural abilities, she runs away to live independently. She fed my tomboy fantasies by living rough, making her own shelter, killing and skinning a large bird, and taming wild animals. Just when she is settling into her new rustic life, disaster strikes. Finally, her talents are recognized by kindly people who whisk her away on dragon-back to a new community of people who can value her for the reasons she values herself.<br /><br />It is not a complicated story, but it is well-told and the theme is universal. It has resonated in my life as I have tried, with only some measure of success, to find a safe place where my own talents are recognized and friends who care for me not in spite of, but because of who I am. The irony for me, of course, is how that place is located in the past, with that dead boy who loved me enough to smuggle books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13419548675623999680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45400990-laura?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2174802509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6103612928796952781">I fell in love with the dragons of Pern and with Anne McCaffrey's writing quite a while back. But I never got to read the Harper Hall trilogy - because my silly old self thought it wouldn't be that good as it's more about harpers and firelizards than dragons!!<br/><br/>My smarter new self now gloats and wants to diligently <s>kick my old silly self's butt</s> preach about assumptions and how we're not really supposed to make them, because they'll probably end up punching us in the face! :D<br/><br/>This book about harpers</span>
  <span id="freeText6103612928796952781" style="display:none">I fell in love with the dragons of Pern and with Anne McCaffrey's writing quite a while back. But I never got to read the Harper Hall trilogy - because my silly old self thought it wouldn't be that good as it's more about harpers and firelizards than dragons!!<br><br>My smarter new self now gloats and wants to diligently <s>kick my old silly self's butt</s> preach about assumptions and how we're not really supposed to make them, because they'll probably end up punching us in the face! :D<br><br>This book about harpers and firelizards was STUNNING! <br><br>I loved Menolly, and her trials made me get spitting mad at times and laugh out loud at others.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559214212i/27592072._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><i>Menolly | Pern Wiki | FANDOM</i><br><br>I could practically picture an old pot flying at a big grumpy dragon's head, who fortunatelly knows to get out of the way <i>on cleaning days</i>! Or a little baby firelizard being grabbed by the tail and unceremoniously dropped in a corner with a juicy piece of meat to <i>stay there and eat</i>! <br><br>Anne McCaffrey has such a way with words that you can really see her stories unfold before your eyes!<br><br>In plain and simple words she'll walk you through a tale of courage and determination of a young girl whose only fault is that of wanting to make music.<br><br>In a world where music is only made by men, because women are not worthy of the honour; in a hold where women need to know their place and do only what they're told; in a family where a daughter is not loved if she doesn't carry her weight according to precepts and tradition, Menolly dares to rebel and follow a dream!<br><br>Intricatelly woven into a culture and lifestyle so different than ours, and yet so alike, Menolly's tale will point out both the best and worst in human nature. It will make you both rage and sigh, and will soften your heart with the gentle touch of the little dragon cousins: not one but lots of pesky, perky firelizards! <br>And how I wish I had a little one of those!!<br><br>A song full of feeling, strength and determination - Dragonsong is one to listen to!<br><br>I highly recommend it!<br>May it lift your spirits the way it did mine!<br>Happy reading! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6103612928796952781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1780853797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11936273045300496838">I've read Dragonsong several times over the years and it continues to be one of my favourite Young Adult novels of all time. Menolly is neither bad-ass warrior nor shrinking violet, but rather someone whose passion for music in all its forms combines with a strong sense of decency to carry her through the trials of living in a place where she's not wanted, and having to make a place for herself outside her familiar home.<br/><br/>Dragonsong neither fits the contemporary notion of Young Adult nor Middle Gr</span>
  <span id="freeText11936273045300496838" style="display:none">I've read Dragonsong several times over the years and it continues to be one of my favourite Young Adult novels of all time. Menolly is neither bad-ass warrior nor shrinking violet, but rather someone whose passion for music in all its forms combines with a strong sense of decency to carry her through the trials of living in a place where she's not wanted, and having to make a place for herself outside her familiar home.<br /><br />Dragonsong neither fits the contemporary notion of Young Adult nor Middle Grade but is instead a kind of timeless story that appealed to me both as a teenager and as an adult. While it does sit within the massive canon of Pern novels, it works perfectly well as a standalone book for those who've never read any of the Dragonriders books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11936273045300496838" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1610576651" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1610576651" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/202724-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601676054p2/202724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1610576651?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Ideiosepius" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Ideiosepius" href="/user/show/4802663-deborah-ideiosepius">Deborah Ideiosepius</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/949118.Dragonsong">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4802663-deborah-ideiosepius?shelf=2017-reading-challenge">2017-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4802663-deborah-ideiosepius?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2038724522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3031892816165406240">The Dragon books were part of the network of books that introduced me in my teen years to fantasy and sci-fi and on re-reading them years later it is encouraging to find them still as well written as I remember them. The plots still as riveting, the world-building still as thrilling and the characters still as good - well, maybe just a tiny bit more teen angst than I look for these days, but otherwise just as good!<br/><br/>In Dragonsong we follow the adventures of Menolly the youngest daughter in a sea h</span>
  <span id="freeText3031892816165406240" style="display:none">The Dragon books were part of the network of books that introduced me in my teen years to fantasy and sci-fi and on re-reading them years later it is encouraging to find them still as well written as I remember them. The plots still as riveting, the world-building still as thrilling and the characters still as good - well, maybe just a tiny bit more teen angst than I look for these days, but otherwise just as good!<br /><br />In Dragonsong we follow the adventures of Menolly the youngest daughter in a sea hold where everyone works brutally hard and which has no appreciation for music. Menolly is all about the music, and when the old hold Harper dies she is slowly pushed to her limits until she leaves the hold completely, to live outside during thread-fall, a thing no one believes is possible. She impresses fire-lizards, small wild, relatives of the massive dragons and then she teaches them to sing.<br /><br />Still as good as when I read it years ago, as good as when it was written in the 1970's , I wonder a little if it could be as amazing to a young girl reading it today as it was to us all back then? We has so few strong women in fiction to enchant us. Well, there is more out there these days, but this one is as good as ever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3031892816165406240" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_24212389" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24212389" />
    <a title="Jon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/899665-jon"><img alt="Jon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375036866p2/899665.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/24212389?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon" href="/user/show/899665-jon">Jon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553258523" href="/book/show/797079.Dragonsong">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone who loves dragons and music. </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899665-jon?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899665-jon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899665-jon?shelf=my-favorites">my-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899665-jon?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899665-jon?shelf=read-in-my-teens">read-in-my-teens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899665-jon?shelf=loved-it">loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/899665-jon?shelf=five-star-favorites">five-star-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer24212389&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24212389" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7624569512868346194">I almost named my daughter Menolly because I loved this book so much. And it would have been a completely appropriate name for her - she is currently in college pursuing a degree in vocal performance and has many musical talents and abilities.<br/><br/>I read this book when I was an adolescent and it struck such a chord with me that I read it and re-read it once or twice a year until I was an adult with children myself. <br/><br/>Menolly is the daughter of a strict practical sea holder on Pern. Her father has littl</span>
  <span id="freeText7624569512868346194" style="display:none">I almost named my daughter Menolly because I loved this book so much. And it would have been a completely appropriate name for her - she is currently in college pursuing a degree in vocal performance and has many musical talents and abilities.<br /><br />I read this book when I was an adolescent and it struck such a chord with me that I read it and re-read it once or twice a year until I was an adult with children myself. <br /><br />Menolly is the daughter of a strict practical sea holder on Pern. Her father has little time or patience for such frivolous activities as music and is very conscience of propriety and everyone's proper place in the social structure of his sea hold. <br /><br />When the sea hold's harper, and Menolly's musical mentor and friend, dies, a replacement is not expected for many months. Menolly's father has a duty to fulfill in the education of the sea hold's children so he reluctantly agrees to let Menolly assume that responsibility temporarily until the new Harper arrives. <br /><br />Menolly instructs the children carefully as her parents expect her to. But her music calls to her incessantly and she can't contain herself completely. She composes and writes a song one afternoon in the classroom after the children have left to do their chores. Unfortunately, her father happens to be passing by in the hall, doesn't recognize the tune, and proceeds to beat Menolly for the audacity of breaking his commandment of "no tuning." <br /><br />Menolly is so devastated by this event, she decides to run away from home. She gathers up some food and clothes and escapes through the front door of the sea hold, leaving it unlocked and open during a Fall (something she had forgot about in her haste to leave). A Fall is the deadly rain from the sky (actually space) that contains a virulent organism that east all things organic in seconds. Only stone, metal or water can protect you from it. The Dragonriders of Pern fly to fight the menace before it can reach the ground, but if the terrain is rocky or watery, they will let it fall. <br /><br />Menolly is trapped on the beach and squirms her way into a small cave where a fire lizard queen and her eggs are hatching. As they hatch, the hungry fire lizards leave the cave only to be destroyed by the Fall outside. Menolly is desparate to save them, so starts feeding them from her supplies. In the end, she saves nine fire lizards and soon discovers that like Dragons, they now "look" to her. <br /><br />Menolly survives for a time on her own, but again is caught out in a Fall and tries to outrun the leading edge. A Dragonrider spots her, thinking she's a boy because she is very tall and lanky, scoops her up and takes her back to the Weir. From that point forward, Menolly's life changes, for the better. <br /><br />Menolly still struggles and is very unsure of herself. Eventually, those around her that care and befriend her draw her out from her harden shell and she eventually finds herself a student in the Harper Hall. <br /><br />This is a great coming of age tale. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7624569512868346194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer208995864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15884635165755050749">There is nothing like snuggling under the covers with one of your favorite books on a rainy day. <br/><br/>I love this book, unconditionally, so don't expect a fair review from me. This is the book that led to my discovery of both sci-fi and fantasy as genres, it opened up the world to me, at the time I was eleven but a decade (+) later I still enjoy it.<br/><br/>The book was written for an arguably younger audience than any other set of books in McCaffrey's Pern series. There is no sex, minimal violence, the readi</span>
  <span id="freeText15884635165755050749" style="display:none">There is nothing like snuggling under the covers with one of your favorite books on a rainy day. <br /><br />I love this book, unconditionally, so don't expect a fair review from me. This is the book that led to my discovery of both sci-fi and fantasy as genres, it opened up the world to me, at the time I was eleven but a decade (+) later I still enjoy it.<br /><br />The book was written for an arguably younger audience than any other set of books in McCaffrey's Pern series. There is no sex, minimal violence, the reading level is definitly geared toward middleschoolers (not in a condescending way though), and the main characters are in their teens. Still, its a necessary part of the Pernverse for any enthusiast.<br /><br />The characters are enjoyable, Harper Hall is a favorite location of mine, everyone wants a firelizard after reading this story, and its a quick but excellent read. I think it says something that I have read this book over a dozen times, but still find myself longing to relive the events therein.<br /><br />Do yourself a favor if its raining out, curl up with any of your favorite books, but I do hope you'll give this one a try.<br /><br />((Read as #100 book of 2012 in celebration of being able to read at all after a few trying years of little time for literature))</span>
  <a data-text-id="15884635165755050749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1360492754" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1360492754" />
    <a title="Susan Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12342015-susan-kennedy"><img alt="Susan Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346263504p2/12342015.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1360492754?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan Kennedy" href="/user/show/12342015-susan-kennedy">Susan Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/41740137-dragonsong">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12342015-susan-kennedy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1360492754&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1360492754" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10913715106294555683">This book focuses on Menolly who lives in a fishing hold. She is talented musically with a fine voice and is able to play many instruments. However, her father does not support her in her talent and in fact tries to hamper her since she is a girl. <br/><br/>Menolly is such a lovely character that I loved the first time I read these and that warm and fuzzy just came back again on the reread. She runs away from the hold and is caught out in threadfall. She takes refuge in a cave during threadfall and there </span>
  <span id="freeText10913715106294555683" style="display:none">This book focuses on Menolly who lives in a fishing hold. She is talented musically with a fine voice and is able to play many instruments. However, her father does not support her in her talent and in fact tries to hamper her since she is a girl. <br /><br />Menolly is such a lovely character that I loved the first time I read these and that warm and fuzzy just came back again on the reread. She runs away from the hold and is caught out in threadfall. She takes refuge in a cave during threadfall and there is a hatching of fire lizards going on. She ends up impressing nine of them to save them from death. She finds herself out in threadfall once again some time later. She is making a run for her shelter when she is rescued by a dragon. She has run her feet raw, so she spends time in the Weyr healing. <br /><br />She is such a great character. She does find her happy ending, but it is through pain and heartache. She is so beaten down emotionally by her mother and father that she has to overcome. She does and it is fabulously written. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10913715106294555683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1761191102" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16882981619753035320">I am a little confused about the order in which I have to read the books of this series because there are different approaches. I chose the order in which they were released. So I have to break the Dragonriders of Pern trilogy to begin this.<br/><br/>In the Harper Hall trilogy we are at the same time as the previous book of the series but we follow a different story. The protagonist of this story is the sweet and sensitive Menolly who goes against the strict conservative beliefs of the region that was bor</span>
  <span id="freeText16882981619753035320" style="display:none">I am a little confused about the order in which I have to read the books of this series because there are different approaches. I chose the order in which they were released. So I have to break the Dragonriders of Pern trilogy to begin this.<br /><br />In the Harper Hall trilogy we are at the same time as the previous book of the series but we follow a different story. The protagonist of this story is the sweet and sensitive Menolly who goes against the strict conservative beliefs of the region that was born expressing her love for music, which in their opinion is a purely male affair. That is why she knows the strong disapproval of hers that reaches the limits of rejection. Disappointed seeks love and appreciation somewhere and finds them in the strangest place. It is the beginning of a very moving, sensitive and emotional story, written in a beautiful way that makes the reader feel all the emotions of the heroine on her journey.<br /><br />  A book that really touched me and from now on will have a special place in my heart.</span>

<div id="review_386815168" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/386815168" />
    <a title="bella" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6827846-bella"><img alt="bella" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430245258p2/6827846.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/386815168?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="bella" class="user" itemprop="url" name="bella" href="/user/show/6827846-bella">bella</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer386815168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8880561575586344412">This is the BEST book I've read this year. I'm actually not sure I can explain my love for this book but I'm going to try. <br/><br/>I've been a little disgruntled with the fantasy genre (especially ya fantasy). I'm not a fan of the over emergence of vampires, fairies and angels. The Game of Thrones helped redeem adult fantasy for me and Dragonsong has totally redeemed my love of ya fantasy. <br/><br/>I never picked up this series as a teen and I wish I had. <br/><br/>Dragonsong is the first book in the Harper Hall trilogy a</span>
  <span id="freeText8880561575586344412" style="display:none">This is the BEST book I've read this year. I'm actually not sure I can explain my love for this book but I'm going to try. <br /><br />I've been a little disgruntled with the fantasy genre (especially ya fantasy). I'm not a fan of the over emergence of vampires, fairies and angels. The Game of Thrones helped redeem adult fantasy for me and Dragonsong has totally redeemed my love of ya fantasy. <br /><br />I never picked up this series as a teen and I wish I had. <br /><br />Dragonsong is the first book in the Harper Hall trilogy and the first Dragonriders of Pern book that I've read. It set around Menolly , who lives in the Sea Hold. She has an extraordinary musical ability, but can never dream of being a Harper because Harpers are always boys. After a accident renders Menolly unable to play music, she runs away from the oppressive Sea Hold and discovers the fire lizards and sets the course for an adventure that will bring her close to the dragons she sings about. <br /><br />I loved Menolly. Despite her oppressive surroundings she finds ways to be positive, like secretly tuning and singing. I felt like I was taking the journey with Menolly. I felt like crying when her hand was injured and she couldn't play. I rejoiced with her when she left the hold, even though she didn't know what the outcome would be. <br /><br />I love the world of Pern that Anne McCaffrey as created. It's pure escapism for me. I got caught up in the world and didn't want to leave. Thankfully there are plenty of Pern novels to discover and I will be diving into Dragonsinger next. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8880561575586344412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16615477949278531626" style="display:none">This was good, but not great.<br /><br />If the book was any longer I might not have felt the need to finish it, but it was just the right combination of length and interesting to make me want to know how it all turned out for the protagonist. <br /><br />The world Anne Mccaffrey created is intriguing, but other than that there was not much happening. In saying that, the second half was much better than the first, and I am almost tempted to carry on with the series, but not sure if I will as there are so many other books clamouring for my attention.</span>

  <span id="freeText7577731215459195883" style="display:none">I didn't particularly enjoy this book, but I don't think it was really the book's fault. It introduced me to the world of Pern and was one of the few things I have ever been able to give back to my Aunt Debbie to repay her for her kindness in introducing me to science-fiction/fantasy, Isaac Asimov, John Bellairs...<br/><br/>Dragonsong serves both as an introduction for young adult readers to the Dragonrider series, an examination of gender roles and tradition in their society (and perhaps in ours), as well as a </span>
  <span id="freeText12946684973784594345" style="display:none">I just reread this for the first time in 17 years... I love this trilogy so much! It introduced me to the world of Pern and was one of the few things I have ever been able to give back to my Aunt Debbie to repay her for her kindness in introducing me to science-fiction/fantasy, Isaac Asimov, John Bellairs...<br /><br />Dragonsong serves both as an introduction for young adult readers to the Dragonrider series, an examination of gender roles and tradition in their society (and perhaps in ours), as well as a loving celebration of music and poetry. It is followed by Dragonsinger and Dragondrums.<br /><br />New readers may take some effort to adjust to McCaffery's Pern dialect and the strange apostrophied names of the male Dragonriders, but this gets easier with time and is an excellent language learning tool. Readers may learn to pick up on implied meanings, for example: the toilet or privy is called "the necessary".<br /><br />Solid storytelling is made even more memorable by vivid views of the landscape of the planet, the social order and a brief history of Pern, and dazzling descriptions of the fanciful wildlife, including dragons and fire lizards. This story will captivate and delight even the most reluctant reader.</span>

<div id="review_300932569" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300932569" />
    <a title="Kent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8341353-kent"><img alt="Kent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332736340p2/8341353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/300932569?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kent" href="/user/show/8341353-kent">Kent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8341353-kent?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8341353-kent?shelf=youthy">youthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8341353-kent?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300932569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13548028418399934830">Alien prejudice is a favorite trope for sci-fi fantasy writers. Presumably, reading about strange discrimination teaches us that all discrimination is strange. Thoughtful writers like Iain Banks can use alien prejudice to comment on the dynamics of power and on cultural relativity. That makes for an interesting read.<br/><br/>In Dragonsong, Anne McCaffrey has done something else entirely. It turns out that a main character who goes against the fake cultural grain can be two things simultaneously: 1. someo</span>
  <span id="freeText13548028418399934830" style="display:none">Alien prejudice is a favorite trope for sci-fi fantasy writers. Presumably, reading about strange discrimination teaches us that all discrimination is strange. Thoughtful writers like Iain Banks can use alien prejudice to comment on the dynamics of power and on cultural relativity. That makes for an interesting read.<br /><br />In Dragonsong, Anne McCaffrey has done something else entirely. It turns out that a main character who goes against the fake cultural grain can be two things simultaneously: 1. someone who is overcoming prejudice in an unfair world, and 2. someone who totally conforms to the prejudices of the target audience.<br /><br />And so we have Menolly, the girl who is really good at music, but girls aren't supposed to be musicians don'tcha know, so shut up Menolly and go chop vegetables. Does Menolly in any way subvert our expectations of what a female fantasy character should be? No. She's innocent, artistic, the forest creatures love her. She's basically Snow White. <br /><br />This is a story of It Gets Better--Menolly goes from a prejudiced society to one that appreciates her for what she is. That's good, and it <i>does</i> get better, kids--even if you don't conform to bigoted Western cultural expectations.<br /><br />Also, this is some bland-ass prose.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13548028418399934830" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_850823" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/850823" />
    <a title="Cecelia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67555-cecelia"><img alt="Cecelia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541627902p2/67555.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/850823?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cecelia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cecelia" href="/user/show/67555-cecelia">Cecelia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer850823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1084510378008252830">Many a woman who found her love of reading early will fondly reminisce about her ‘horse period’ – when she read anything she could get her hands on that had to do with horses, such as the Marguerite Henry books (Misty of Chincoteague!) and Black Beauty. There’s a smaller and more select group that can reminisce about their ‘dragon period.’ I say this because I know: I went through both. However, unlike horses, my love of dragons and dragon-lore has lasted well into adulthood. And those early dra</span>
  <span id="freeText1084510378008252830" style="display:none">Many a woman who found her love of reading early will fondly reminisce about her ‘horse period’ – when she read anything she could get her hands on that had to do with horses, such as the Marguerite Henry books (Misty of Chincoteague!) and Black Beauty. There’s a smaller and more select group that can reminisce about their ‘dragon period.’ I say this because I know: I went through both. However, unlike horses, my love of dragons and dragon-lore has lasted well into adulthood. And those early dragon books that I devoured were written by the likes of Jane Yolen, Patricia C. Wrede and Anne McCaffrey. <br /><br />Dragonsong is the first book in McCaffrey’s Harper Hall trilogy, a set of sci-fi books for younger readers – today we’d probably call them middle grade. The series is set on the planet Pern, where colonists fight the life-threatening Thread that falls from space with dragonfire (it’s all explained in less fantastic terms than that in the book, trust me). The story follows gifted musician Menolly, youngest daughter of the head of fishing-centric Half Circle Hold, as she struggles against the restrictions of Hold life and traditions that state that women cannot be Harpers. The injustice finally becomes too much and Menolly flees, only to discover a nest of fire lizards, a new life, and a destiny that will take her far from anything she has ever known.<br /> <br />Oh, this book. I must have gotten it at a Scholastic book sale or similar, because I distinctly remember that I bought it because: DRAGONS! and also because there was a $1.99 sale sticker on the front cover. And then, after I was swept into the world of Pern and dragons and fire lizards, I discovered it was the first in a trilogy and had to read the next two immediately. Thank goodness for libraries. <br /><br />The main thing I remember feeling when I read this as a child was just how unfair life was for Menolly. Rereading it now as an adult I still feel the injustice of her situation, even to the point of tears – but it is tempered now with knowledge. Menolly’s life is narrow because she lives on a colonized planet, in a very traditional community, and there are no options for, or knowledge of, anything different. Her family forbids her musical tinkering not solely out of spite, as I thought when I was younger, but out of fear. Half Circle Hold is a patriarchal, sexist society that doesn’t know how to change for the better, so it keeps a stranglehold on Menolly. And it is that attitude that eventually forces her flight into the unknown.<br /> <br />Of course, that flight is what saves Menolly, but it also breaks her spirit and effectively cuts her off from the past. This is one of the clearest examples I can think of in fantasy and science fiction of leaving the past and pushing into the future. It’s an effective narrative to be sure, but I now also think of it as a metaphor for all sci-fi: leaving the repressive, traditional world of the past and pressing on into the future and new and greater heights.<br /> <br />But I mentioned dragons! Well, I’ll deliver (to a degree). Menolly encounters fire lizards, the dragons’ smaller cousins, and these tiny creatures are not only her personal salvation, but they are also her introduction to the life she was meant to live – with enlightened friends and the possibility to follow her musical dreams. I won’t say any more about the book, as you should just read it yourself. It’s wonderful, and for all ages.<br /> <br />Recommended for: fans of adventurous middle grade fiction, those who enjoy (or would like a well-written introduction to) science fiction and fantasy, and anyone who missed their ‘dragon period’ and needs to make up for lost time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1084510378008252830" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3461413939" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3461413939" />
    <a title="John_Dishwasher" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44246464-john-dishwasher"><img alt="John_Dishwasher" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543641832p2/44246464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3461413939?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John_Dishwasher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John_Dishwasher" href="/user/show/44246464-john-dishwasher">John_Dishwasher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3461413939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10491087715839648866">There is a greatness in us that is repressed and even punished by society. Society would have us be machines instead of souls. There may be no better way to demonstrate this in a story than to take the most repressed personality of a culture and give that personality that culture’s most cherished talents. That's what McCaffrey does here. This is not a political statement book, but a sort of medieval fantasy set on another world. So the repression isn't cruel, but it is unequivocal, exacting and </span>
  <span id="freeText10491087715839648866" style="display:none">There is a greatness in us that is repressed and even punished by society. Society would have us be machines instead of souls. There may be no better way to demonstrate this in a story than to take the most repressed personality of a culture and give that personality that culture’s most cherished talents. That's what McCaffrey does here. This is not a political statement book, but a sort of medieval fantasy set on another world. So the repression isn't cruel, but it is unequivocal, exacting and scarring. And the protagonist’s gifts are just as unequivocal and inspiring and resilient. When I grabbed this book out of our living room library my wife mused that it was mostly a young woman’s book. But all of us want to run away and be ourselves when the machinery enforcers come around. I cheered on the 15-year-old protagonist’s claiming of herself, and could identify with it easily. McCaffrey has a gift for narration even if her prose is unadventurous and occasionally dialogue-starved. In chapter 7 of this book she finds a rhythm at the paragraph level that I've not before experienced. I actually re-read that chapter after finishing to make sure I wasn't imagining it. <br /><br />3.5 stars rounded down mostly because this is part one of a trilogy. While the story arrives at a satisfying and even moving resolution, thematically the book is anti-climactic. Probably that will be remedied in book three.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10491087715839648866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Reread this today and it was every bit as good today, perhaps even better. I understand the craft of writing a bit better now, and can say that Anne was a true master storyteller. All ages and lovers of good stories will appreciate this story of wonderful Menolly and her journey towards Harper Hall.</span>

    <a title="The FountainPenDiva, Old school geek chick and lover of teddy bears" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2142927-the-fountainpendiva-old-school-geek-chick-and-lover-of-teddy-bears"><img alt="The FountainPenDiva, Old school geek chick and lover of teddy bears" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584827425p2/2142927.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553120448" href="/book/show/28543.Dragonsong">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2142927-the-fountainpendiva-old-school-geek-chick-and-lover-of-teddy-bears?shelf=characters-musicians">characters-musicians</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49790918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15398535303458918481">There are times I just need to return to those comfort books which have been my companions and best friends through good times and bad times. There are books which, like fine wine, mellow with age. Characters I still love. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28543.Dragonsong__Pern_Harper_Hall___1_' title='Dragonsong (Pern Harper Hall, #1) by Anne McCaffrey' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dragonsong</a> remains one of those stories that still brings a smile to my face and the warm fuzzies to my heart. It's one of the many books that cemented my love of fantasy. <br/><br/>I still remember how it struck such a deep chord within me, the very first time I read it. Menolly's tria</span>
  <span id="freeText15398535303458918481" style="display:none">There are times I just need to return to those comfort books which have been my companions and best friends through good times and bad times. There are books which, like fine wine, mellow with age. Characters I still love. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28543.Dragonsong__Pern_Harper_Hall___1_" title="Dragonsong (Pern Harper Hall, #1) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonsong</a> remains one of those stories that still brings a smile to my face and the warm fuzzies to my heart. It's one of the many books that cemented my love of fantasy. <br /><br />I still remember how it struck such a deep chord within me, the very first time I read it. Menolly's trials were very much like my own, though my family wasn't quite as bad as hers. Still I could relate to that age-old quandary of feeling out of place and unappreciated for possessing gifts that people don't always understand. <br /><br />Menolly, the youngest daughter of a prominent Sea Holder, is musically gifted, a gift that her stern and hidebound parents disapprove of. Forbidden to even play, much less sing, she decides to run away and live holdless rather than suffer one more day without what she loves. While Menolly is sensitive, she's also resourceful. She survives and even begins to thrive in a sea cave with nine fire lizards (genetic cousins to the great dragons of Pern) for company. I remember really hating her parents back then, especially her mother. With the lens of maturity I understand why they behaved the way they did, but still, to treat their daughter like a pariah doesn't sit well at all. However, Menolly got the last laugh. <br /><br />I actually wrote the beginnings of a fan fic where Menolly becomes the Masterharper. <br /><br />Like its companion series <u>The Dragonriders of Pern</u>, this is a classic series that lives and breathes. Another masterwork from a grand mistress of fantasy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15398535303458918481" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4445117306461836590">Over the years I have heard great things about this series, but just never got around to it. I finally picked up this book, and now I see what everyone was talking about. It was fantastic!!!! Pern has lived in fear of the Thread for centuries. During threadfall, it falls from the sky and anyone or anything in its path will be burnt up. The main thing that can stop it is fire. So the dragonriders mount up and stop it every threadfall. Living in her sea hold, Menolly doesn't worry much about the t</span>
  <span id="freeText4445117306461836590" style="display:none">Over the years I have heard great things about this series, but just never got around to it. I finally picked up this book, and now I see what everyone was talking about. It was fantastic!!!! Pern has lived in fear of the Thread for centuries. During threadfall, it falls from the sky and anyone or anything in its path will be burnt up. The main thing that can stop it is fire. So the dragonriders mount up and stop it every threadfall. Living in her sea hold, Menolly doesn't worry much about the thread. All she wants is to become a Harper and create her own songs to sing. But, girls can't be harpers. According to her father, she is a disgrace. With nothing left to lose, she leaves her hold and starts a new life in a cave. Tons of adventures are in store for her! This book was great! I love Menolly and wanted to kick her dad's a** for the way he acted. </span>

<div id="review_1247150337" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1247150337" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1247150337?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1247150337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15008652698828123288">I'm not usually a fan of dragon stories, but when my aunt bought me this book, within the first few pages I was hooked on it. Menolly is a memorable character and the book has themes of friendship, bravery and kindness without getting too preachy about it. The author's writing style is amazing and all in all, this is a great book for all ages, I highly recommend it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1426589018" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1426589018" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6074441-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352692366p2/6074441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1426589018?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/6074441-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6074441-beth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6074441-beth?shelf=fantasy-by-women">fantasy-by-women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6074441-beth?shelf=1970s-sff-by-women">1970s-sff-by-women</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1426589018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9255050164803842821">I've had this book forever, but had never actually read it, and it ended up being a short book for a busy month, as well as fitting in with several of my reading projects: (1) YA (2) books owned but unread for literally decades (3) older SF and fantasy by women (before 2000 or so). This one is from 1978.<br/><br/>I will start by apologizing to anyone who loved this book as a kid and who remains fond of it today....<br/> <br/>I'm sorry. <br/><br/>Well, let's press on.<br/><br/>Life in Half-Circle Hold on Pern is dour and humorless, Pur</span>
  <span id="freeText9255050164803842821" style="display:none">I've had this book forever, but had never actually read it, and it ended up being a short book for a busy month, as well as fitting in with several of my reading projects: (1) YA (2) books owned but unread for literally decades (3) older SF and fantasy by women (before 2000 or so). This one is from 1978.<br /><br />I will start by apologizing to anyone who loved this book as a kid and who remains fond of it today....<br /> <br />I'm sorry. <br /><br />Well, let's press on.<br /><br />Life in Half-Circle Hold on Pern is dour and humorless, Puritanical in feel without any convincing justification for it in the text. There's no laughter in the face of trouble, here--Thread is serious business. The sole concession to amusement in a life otherwise 100% devoted to communal labor is the Harper, and he (always he, of course) only has a place at the Hold because he teaches the children history and the Pern code of conduct through a preapproved roster of songs. <br /><br />Fifteen-year-old Menolly's family has no affection for its youngest daughter; none of them has a kind word to say to or about her, and have nothing better to do with their spare time than to police her to make sure she isn't composing music, 'cause only dudes are allowed to do that. She has perfect pitch, and can play any instrument like a virtuoso with very little practice. But that isn't important.... Oh no, she hummed something non-canonical! Whip her with a belt! <br /><br />These jerks all but dance with glee when Menolly injures her hand so badly she nearly loses it, leaving her "crippled"--oh, you, '70s!--and unable to play musical instruments. (And we later find her mother may have <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[deliberately sabotaged her hand's healing so she wouldn't be able to play <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. What a bunch of assholes.) Later, when Menolly runs away from the hold, they don't worry or grieve, even though she could be dead to a recent incursion of Thread. They shrug and say she didn't toe the line, so it's her own stupid fault. <br /><br />Thank goodness, after running away, Menolly finds affection and understanding in a newly-hatched nest of small dragon-like creatures called fire lizards. She Impresses (with a capital "I" because Important World-Building Concepts are Capitalized in this World) all nine of the lizards who live through the hatching, and spends many happy days singing to and feeding them.<br /><br />Menolly finds her way to one of the dragon Weyrs when a dragonrider rescues her from another Thread attack. The Weyr is full of overbearing and snippy people, but at least they don't treat her like poo on their shoes, and they're open-minded about scandalous things like women performing art. They even offer to let her stay there forever.<br /><br />As sarcastic as I am about <i>Dragonsong</i> here, this was enjoyable to read. Not so much in the first half, since I found the presentation of the Half-Circle Hold folk ham-handed and unconvincing. I felt an affinity for the Benden Weyr people, though, or at least their easygoing culture, which, similar to the general vibe of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6320099-crystal-singer" rel="nofollow noopener">Crystal Singer</a> which I read a year or two ago, has a lot of congenial hanging out in between the hard work (not to mention copious amounts of alcohol). Reminds me of my own young adulthood right after college, actually.<br /><br />I couldn't really tell the Benden Weyr people apart, with T'This and T'That and T'Other, and Semolina and Purina and Bologna (I'm making these up, of course, but the men's and women's names follow this general pattern), and I'm guessing that if you've read the earlier books in the Pern series, you'll recognize familiar characters in Weyr Benden.<br /><br />There's a convincing sense of ecology to Pern, and of a society where the smaller settlements have had to revert to hunting and gathering, since staying in the open can be deadly to people, domesticated animals, and crops. Menolly can use outdoors skills to feed both herself and her fire lizard friends when she runs away, but on the downside is lacking in means to make her own shoes and clothing. So that was a cool detail. Also, the areas around Half-Circle Hold, and Benden Weyr itself, had a real sense of place for me. Although, as someone steeped in the U.S.'s car culture, I wonder how large of an area the map in the front of the book actually covers. At times, I thought you could easily walk from one settlement to another in a day, which made me confused when the dragons needed to teleport between settlements rather than just flying.<br /><br />There are ways in which <i>Dragonsong</i> feels old; it's younger than I am, and <i>I'm</i> not old, so I'm not sure what's going on, there. (Heh, heh.) Menolly doesn't seem as beholden to men as <i>Crystal Singer</i>'s Killashandra did, and there's Lessa at Benden Weyr to mitigate the idea that it's only men who are ever in charge on Pern, so I think it's McCaffrey's writing style, heavy in adverbs*, that gives it that old-school feeling. Or the unabashed use of storytelling elements--such as psychic bonds with hyper-intelligent animals--that may have been stylish at the time, but are embarrassing to wear in public today. It isn't McCaffrey's fault I read this almost 40 years after it came out.<br /><br />*I'm not entirely on board with the current notion that prose pruned of all adverbs and adjectives is superior, but here things have gone too far in the other direction.<br /><br />I'm kind of sorry that I ignored <i>Dragonsong</i>, or even found it boring, when I was of an age to appreciate it, since my cynicism makes me unable to connect with ultra-talented Menolly and her adorable little pets who somehow understand human speech and gestures from birth. Or the idea that the world might fall all over itself to take care of one lone girl in her time of need and give her a kind home and the recognition she deserves.<br /><br />Despite everything, McCaffrey kept me turning the pages and I'm interested in reading more about Pern. It isn't hard to see why she was a bestseller in her day. She was a fine storyteller.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9255050164803842821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

	<tr>
		<td>
		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FTwzi3JILtHKzx9n5dUN5gOasoKC6dKPlzZF5wnmPwAvGlpZyRbnuW3kqwYSIAc51cVVSkxkXOjMSANWxKXNmg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('H5fQQptXYLatBbWa5hbeQZgKRgHM7qxxxNeYllzgPpQlsbmQIAmp3gouAfsR49SeTlWhyQJjIhafqd4nkaPMDg==')})
  }

As the author of the &quot;Dragonriders of Pern&quot; series, McCaffrey (b. 1926) was one of the most significant writers of science fiction and fantasy. She was the first woman to win the Hugo and Nebula awards, and her 1978 novel &quot;The White Dragon&quot; was the first science-fiction novel to appear on the New York Times hardcover bestseller list. \n\nThis biography reveals a fascinating and complex figure, one who created and re-created her fiction by drawing on life experiences. At various stages, McCaffrey was a beautiful young girl who refused to fit into traditional gender roles in high school, a restless young mother who wanted to write, an American expatriate who became an Irish citizen, an animal lover who dreamed of fantasy worlds with perfect relationships between humans and beasts, and a wife trapped in an unhappy marriage just as the women\'s movement took hold. \n\nAuthor Robin Roberts conducted interviews with McCaffrey, her children, friends, and colleagues, and used archival correspondence and contemporary reviews and criticism. The biography examines how McCaffrey\'s early interests in theater, Slavonic languages and literature, and British history, mythology, and culture all shaped her science fiction. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12441600203612809230">Anne McCaffrey was born on April 1st, 1926, in Cambridge, Massachusetts.<br/><br/>Her parents were George Herbert McCaffrey, BA, MA PhD (Harvard), Colonel USA Army (retired), and Anne Dorothy McElroy McCaffrey, estate agent. She had two brothers: Hugh McCaffrey (deceased 1988), Major US Army, and Kevin Richard McCaffrey, still living.<br/><br/>Anne was educated at Stuart Hall in Staunton Virginia, Montclair High Scho</span>
  <span id="freeText12441600203612809230" style="display:none">Anne McCaffrey was born on April 1st, 1926, in Cambridge, Massachusetts.<br /><br />Her parents were George Herbert McCaffrey, BA, MA PhD (Harvard), Colonel USA Army (retired), and Anne Dorothy McElroy McCaffrey, estate agent. She had two brothers: Hugh McCaffrey (deceased 1988), Major US Army, and Kevin Richard McCaffrey, still living.<br /><br />Anne was educated at Stuart Hall in Staunton Virginia, Montclair High School in Montclair, New Jersey, and graduated cum laude from Radcliffe College, majoring in Slavonic Languages and Literatures.<br /><br />Her working career included Liberty Music Shops and Helena Rubinstein (1947-1952). She married in 1950 and had three children: Alec Anthony, b. 1952, Todd, b.1956, and Georgeanne, b.1959.<br /><br />Anne McCaffrey’s first story was published by Sam Moskowitz in Science Fiction + Magazine and her first novel was published by Ballantine Books in 1967. By the time the three children of her marriage were comfortably in school most of the day, she had already achieved enough success with short stories to devote full time to writing. Her first novel, Restoree, was written as a protest against the absurd and unrealistic portrayals of women in s-f novels in the 50s and early 60s. It is, however, in the handling of broader themes and the worlds of her imagination, particularly the two series The Ship Who Sang and the fourteen novels about the Dragonriders of Pern that Ms. McCaffrey’s talents as a story-teller are best displayed.<br /><br />She died at the age of 85, after suffering a massive stroke on 21 November 2011.<br /><br />Obituaries: <a href="http://www.locusmag.com/News/2011/11/anne-mccaffrey-1926-2011/" rel="nofollow noopener">Locus</a>, <a href="http://www.mediabistro.com/galleycat/anne-mccaffrey-has-died_b42826" rel="nofollow noopener">GalleyCat</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12441600203612809230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
